deploy web applications remotely to a shared repository that is distributed across the cluster. This feature allows you to deploy once to any triad server and have the application be updated automatically across the entire cluster. When a new dynamic server joins the cluster, the triad will populate it with these applications as well.</p> <p>Web Deploy waræ–‡ä»¶å¤§æ¦‚æ˜¯ä»4.0.0å¼€å§‹æ”¯æŒçš„ï¼Œä¸è¿‡æƒ³è¦åœ¨Web deployä¸€ä¸ªåº”ç”¨ä¹Ÿä¸æ˜¯ä¸€ä»¶ç®€å•çš„äº‹æƒ…ï¼Œé¦–å…ˆå¾—å…ˆè¿›å…¥åå°ã€‚ç„¶åè¿˜å¾—ä»¥Httpsæ–¹å¼è®¿é—®ã€‚ä¸è¿‡å‘½ä»¤è¡Œä¸‹éƒ¨ç½²å°±æ²¡é‚£æ²¡æ³•éº»çƒ¦ã€‚Resin3å¾—æ‰‹åŠ¨é…ç½®web-app-deployã€‚ æœ€ç®€å•çš„ä½†åˆä¸çˆ½åŠæ³•å°±æ˜¯æƒ³åŠæ³•æŠŠwaræ–‡ä»¶ä¸Šä¼ åˆ°resin-pro-3.1.13webappsç›®å½•ä¸‹ï¼Œä¼šè‡ªåŠ¨éƒ¨ç½²ï¼ˆå°±ç®—Resinå·²å¯åŠ¨ä¹Ÿä¼šè‡ªåŠ¨éƒ¨ç½²ï¼Œä¸å½±å“å·²éƒ¨ç½²çš„åº”ç”¨ï¼‰ã€‚</p> <p>Resin3éƒ¨ç½²è¯¦æƒ…ï¼š<a href="http://www.caucho.com/resin-3.1/doc/webapp-deploy.xtp" target="_blank"><a href="http://www.caucho.com/resin-3.1/doc/webapp-deploy.xtp">http://www.caucho.com/resin-3.1/doc/webapp-deploy.xtp</a></a></p> <p>Resin4éƒ¨ç½²Waræ–‡ä»¶è¯¦æƒ…ï¼š<a href="http://www.caucho.com/resin-4.0/admin/deploy.xtp" target="_blank"><a href="http://www.caucho.com/resin-4.0/admin/deploy.xtp">http://www.caucho.com/resin-4.0/admin/deploy.xtp</a></a></p> <p>Resin4è¿›å…¥åå°åé€‰æ‹©Deploy,ä¸è¿‡è¿˜å¾—ç”¨SSLæ–¹å¼è¯·æ±‚ã€‚Resinè¦èµ°ä¸€ä¸ªâ€éåŠ å¯†é€šé“â€ã€‚</p> <p>To deploy an application remotely: log into the resin-admin console on any triad server. Make sure you are connecting over SSL, as this feature is not available over a non-encrypted channel. Browse to the "webapp" tab of the resin-admin server and at the bottom of the page, enter the virtual host, URL, and local .war file specifying the web application, then press "Deploy". The application should now be deployed on the server. In a few moments, all the servers in the cluster will have the webapp.</p> <p>ï¿¼<img src="http://static.wooyun.org/20130922/2013092207565886704.png" alt="enter image description here"></p> Attacks/tools</h1> <p><a href=""></a><a href=""></a></p> <ul> <li><p><strong>What's new in DDoS?</strong></p> </li> <li><p><a href="http://www.cert.org/reports/dsit_workshop.pdf" target="_blank">Nothing, really.</a> (Some people are just late to the party. ;)<a href=""></a></p> </li> <li><p>Anonymous threatens reflected/amplified attack on the DNS Root name servers</p> </li> <li><p><a href="http://pastebin.com/NKbnh8q8" target="_blank">Threat by Anonymous to take down the Internet by a reflected DDoS attack against the DNS root name servers</a>, Pastebin posting, February 12, 2012</p> </li> <li><a href="http://www.cricketondns.com/post.cfm/could-a-ddos-attack-against-the-roots-succeed" target="_blank">Could a DDoS Attack Against the Roots Succeed?"</a>, by Cricket Liu, March 13, 2012</li> <li><a href="https://www.dns-oarc.net/wiki/mitigating-dns-denial-of-service-attacks" target="_blank">Mitigating DNS Denial of Service Attacks</a>, DNS OARC</li> <li><p>What is a distributed reflected DDoS attack?</p> </li> <li><p>Distributed reflected DoS attacks go back to 2001. See the sections below for information on <a href="http://staff.washington.edu/dittrich/misc/ddos/#drdos" target="_blank">DRDoS examples and background</a> and <a href="http://staff.washington.edu/dittrich/misc/ddos/#fundamentals" target="_blank">fundamental problems</a>.</p> </li> <li><a href="http://lists.jammed.com/ISN/2006/03/0085.html" target="_blank">Security Experts Warn of Devastating Web Attack</a>, ISN, March 21, 2006</li> <li><a href="http://securityskeptic.typepad.com/the-security-skeptic/the-worrisome-threat-of-dns-ddos-amplification-attacks.html" target="_blank">The Worrisome Threat of DNS DDoS Amplification Attacks</a>, The Security Skeptic [This article was originally published in the ENISA Quarterly, 6 June 2006. It is no longer available from ENISA.]</li> <li><p>Have the root servers been attacked before?</p> </li> <li><p><a Attack</a>, by K-ROOT, February, 2007</li> <li><a href="http://ddos.arbornetworks.com/2007/06/february-2007-root-server-attacks-a-qualitative-report/" target="_blank">February 2007 Root Server Attacks computer</a>, by Mark Clayton, The Christian Science Monitor, December 9, 2010</li> <li><a href="http://www.csmonitor.com/USA/2010/1209/Anonymous-How-dangerous-is-hacker-network-defending-WikiLeaks" Apps, Reuters, December 10, 2010</li> <li><a href="http://thesop.org/story/20101210/operation-payback-is-becoming-a-complete-failure.html" target="_blank">Operation Payback is Becoming a Complete Failure</a>, by John Danz, December 10, 2010</li> <li><p>Are the Anonymous "Operation Payback" attacks a form of "civil disobedience?" Read these carefully, then you decide.</p> </li> <li><p><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retributive_justice" target="_blank">Retributive justice</a>, Wikipedia</p> </li> <li><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incitement" target="_blank">Incitement</a>, Wikepedia</li> <li><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_Disobedience" target="_blank">Civil Disobedience</a>, Wikipedia</li> </ul> <p><a href=""></a></p> <ul> <li><strong>Some General Subjects/Themes</strong></li> </ul> <p><a href=""></a></p> <ul> <li><p>Distributed Reflected DNS attacks (and some background)</p> </li> <li><p>Randal Vaughn and Gadi Evron released an analysis of <a href="http://www.isotf.org/news/DNS-Amplification-Attacks.pdf" target="_blank">DNS Amplification Attacks</a> (which use distributed reflection and amplification) on March 17, 2006</p> </li> <li><a href="http://www.theinquirer.net/?article=30361" target="_blank">VeriSign reports a "new DDoS attack"</a> in an article published March 17, 2006</li> <li><a href="http://www.us-cert.gov/reading_room/DNS-recursion121605.pdf" target="_blank">CERT/CC publishes a document discussing DNS recursion problems and some solutions for preventing becoming a reflector</a> in early 2006.</li> <li><a href="http://www.gossamer-threads.com/lists/nanog/users/89657" target="_blank">NANOG Thread "DNS deluge for x.p.ctrc.cc"</a> from February 2006</li> <li>Distributed reflected DDoS attacks are covered on pages 19-20, 45, 51-52, and 297 in <a href="http://vig.prenhall.com/catalog/academic/product/0,1144,0131475738,00.html" target="_blank">Internet Denial of Service: Attack and Defense Mechanisms</a>, published in 2005</li> <li>Vern Paxson wrote a paper, <a href="http://www.icir.org/vern/papers/reflectors.CCR.01/reflectors.html" target="_blank">An Analysis of Using Reflectors for Distributed Denial-of-Service Attacks</a>, warning of these kinds of attacks in June 2001</li> <li>A DNS reflection attack on Register.com was publicly discussed in a <a href="http://staff.washington.edu/dittrich/misc/ddos/register.com-unisog.txt" target="_blank">thread on the UNISOG mailing list</a> in January 2001. This attack, which forged requests for the MX records of AOL.com (to amplify the attack) lasted about a week before it could be traced back to all attacking hosts and shut off. It used a large list of DNS servers at least a year old (at the time of the attack.)</li> <li>The Honeynet Project <a href="http://project.honeynet.org/reverse/results/" target="_blank">Reverse Challenge</a>, done in July 2002, involved analysis of a piece of malware that was [not?] surprisingly a DDoS agent. It implemented several DNS related attacks, including a reflection attack.</li> <li>One of the fundamental issues in distributed reflected attacks is the ability of an attacker to spoof source addresses on packets. Documents describing this problem, and suggested fixes, are found in the <a href="http://staff.washington.edu/dittrich/misc/ddos/#mitigation" target="_blank">Mitigation section of this page</a> below, some going back to 2000.</li> <li><a href="https://www.dns-oarc.net/wiki/mitigating-dns-denial-of-service-attacks" target="_blank">Mitigating DNS Denial of Service Attacks</a>, DNS OARC</li> <li><p>Estonia claims to be under cyberwarfare DDoS attack from Russia?</p> </li> <li><p><a href="http://blog.wired.com/defense/2009/03/pro-kremlin-gro.html" target="_blank">Kremlin Kids: We Launched the Estonian Cyber War</a>, by Noah Shachtman, Danger Room blog, Wired.com, March 11, 2009</p> </li> <li><a href="http://www.theregister.co.uk/2009/03/11/russian_admits_estonian_ddos/" target="_blank">Kremlin-backed youths launched Estonian cyberwar, says Russian official</a>, by Dan Goodin, The Register, March 11, 2009</li> <li><a href="http://www.economist.com/world/europe/displaystory.cfm?story_id=9163598" target="_blank">Estonia and Russia: A cyber-riot</a>, The Economist, May 10, 2007</li> <li><a href="http://www.smh.com.au/news/Technology/Estonia-urges-firm-EU-NATO-response-to-new-form-of-warfarecyberattacks/2007/05/16/1178995207414.html" target="_blank">Estonia urges firm EU, NATO response to new form of warfare: cyber-attacks</a>, Sydney Morning Herald, May 16, 2007</li> <li><a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2007/05/18/AR2007051802122.html" target="_blank">Cyber Assaults on Estonia Typify a New Battle Tactic</a>, by Peter Finn, Washington Post Foreign Service, May 19, 2007</li> <li><a href="http://asert.arbornetworks.com/2007/05/estonian-ddos-attacks-a-summary-to-date/" target="_blank">Estonian DDoS Attacks - A summary to date</a>, by Jose Nazario, ArborSERT blog, May 21, 2007</li> <li><a href="http://news.com.com/When+cyberattacks+are+politically+motivated/2008-7349_3-6186751.html" target="_blank">When cyberattacks are politically motivated</a>, by Robert Vamosi, Special to CNET News.com, May 29, 2007 [Interview with Jose Nazario of Arbor Networks]</li> <li><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2007/05/29/technology/29estonia.html" target="_blank">After Computer Siege in Estonia, War Fears Turn to Cyberspace</a>, by Mark Landler and John Markoff, The New York Times, May 29, 2007</li> <li><a href="http://www.cbw.cz/phprs/2007061112.html" target="_blank">Cyberwar is breaking out of sci-fi genre</a>, Pavla Kozkov, Czech Business Weekly, June 11, 2007</li> <li><p>The "Botmaster Underground" case</p> </li> <li><p><a href="http://www.cnn.com/2005/TECH/11/04/crime.botmaster.reut/index.html" target="_blank">FBI agents bust 'Botmaster'</a>, Reuters News Service, November 4, 2005</p> </li> <li><a href="http://news.zdnet.com/2100-1009_22-6030270.html" target="_blank">'Botmaster' pleads guilty to computer crimes</a>, Reuters, January 24, 2006 [Teen admits to controlling somewhere near 500,000 computers, must return $60,000 cash, computer equipment, and a BMW he bought with proceeds from renting the botnet.</li> <li><a href="http://blog.eweek.com/blogs/eweek/archive/2005/11/08/2410.aspx" target="_blank">eWeek blog entry</a> about the case</li> <li><a href="http://www.usdoj.gov/criminal/cybercrime/anchetaArrest.htm" target="_blank">U.S. Department of Justice press release</a>.</li> <li><a href="http://www.outlookseries.com/news/Security/5501.htm" target="_blank">Lee Graham Walker, Axel Gembe CHARGED in Operation Cyberslam</a>, Outlook Series, October 6, 2008</li> <li><a href="http://news.findlaw.com/hdocs/docs/cyberlaw/usanchetaind.pdf" target="_blank">U.S. v. James Jeanson Ancheta</a> (federal indictment)</li> <li><a href="http://news.zdnet.com/2100-1009_22-6070020.html" target="_blank">20-year-old 'botmaster' faces years behind bars</a>, Reuters, May 9, 2006</li> <li><p>This was <em>not</em> the first case of DDoS-for-hire in the U.S., however. That was another case in 2005.</p> </li> <li><p><a href="http://www.fbi.gov/page2/april05/hiredhacker041805.htm" target="_blank">THE CASE OF THE HIRED HACKER: Entrepreneur and Hacker Arrested for
